Chapter 18. ACE Station Keeping

Table of Contents

Objective and Overview
Prerequisites
Mission Description
Resource, Mission, and Output trees
Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree
Objects Required
Creating and Modifying Objects
Creating and Configuring the Mission Sequence
Running the Mission

This tutorial was started from the default settings in the June 9, 2008 build of GMAT.

Objective and Overview

ACE, or Advanced Composition Explorer, studies the Sun and is one of only a few spacecraft that resides at the Sun-Earth L1 Libration Point in a Lissajous Orbit that is quasi-periodic. This tutorial will show the method in which a spacecraft may be station kept at this point in space. Put simply, a number of orbits about the Libration point will be simulated, with each being corrected slightly by small maneuvers due to the unstable nature of Sun-Earth L1.

Download the script file: ACEStationKeepingTutorial.script

Prerequisites

  • Basic Understanding of Libration Point Station Keeping

  • Tutorials:

    • Creating and Propagating a Spacecraft

    • Designing a Hohman Transfer

  • Objects:

    • Spacecraft Object

    • Impulsive Burn Object

    • Propagator Object

    • Barycenter Object

    • Libration Point Object

    • Differential Corrector Object

    • OpenGL Plot Object

    • ReportFile

    • Variable Object

    • Coordinate System Objects

  • Commands:

    • Report Command

    • Equation Command

    • For Command

    • Target Command

    • Vary Command

    • Maneuver Command

    • Propagate Command

    • Achieve Command

Mission Description

  • Objective: Maintain an orbit about the Sun-Earth L1 Libration point by performing a burn perpendicular to the direction of travel so that as the spacecraft passes through the ecliptic, its velocity relative to the Sun and Earth is zero.

  • Assume:

    • A preexisting orbit with given initial conditions

    • A UTCGregorian Epoch of 09 Dec 2005 12:59:60.000

  • Find: The deltaV required perpendicular to the direction of travel at each pass of the ecliptic to meet the above objective

Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Figure: ACE Resource, Mission, and Output Trees

Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree

This section will outline exactly what resources are required to complete the mission outlined within this tutorial. One spacecraft, a single burn to control that spacecraft, and a simple propagator, will be needed. To better see and analyze the spacecraft's motions, we will also need several Plots/Reports, Variable Object, and Coordinate Systems.

Objects Required

  • Spacecraft: ACE

  • Burns: dV

  • Propagators: defaultProp (modified)

  • Solar System: DefaultBC, ESL1

  • Solvers: DefaultDC

  • Plots/Reports: L1View, EarthSunRotView, ESL1Ephem

  • Variables: TotaldV, VX, VY, VZ, dVX, dVY, dVZ, I

  • Coordinate Systems: EarthSunL1CS, EarthSunRotCS

Creating and Modifying Objects

  • Spacecraft

    • Rename DefaultSC to ACE

    • Change the Epoch Format to UTCGregorian

    • Set the Epoch to 09 Dec 2005 12:59:60.000

    • Set X = -528665.5773210001, Y = -1325445.164527, Z = -525969.843578, VX = 0.240435056, VY = -0.068342458, and VZ = 0.0315715361

    Script Syntax:

    Create ((Spacecraft Object)) ACE;
GMAT ACE.DateFormat = UTCGregorian;
GMAT ACE.Epoch = '09 Dec 2005 12:59:60.000';
GMAT ACE.X = -528665.5773210001;
GMAT ACE.Y = -1325445.164527;
GMAT ACE.Z = -525969.843578;
GMAT ACE.VX = 0.240435056;
GMAT ACE.VY = -0.068342458;
GMAT ACE.VZ = 0.0315715361;

    Figure: ACE Spacecraft Object Object

  • Propagators

    • Change the Min Step Size to 9.999999999999999e-022

    • Change the Max Step Size to 86400

    • Change the Max Step Attempts to 100

    • Remove any Primary Bodies

    • Add Sun, Earth, and Luna as Point Masses

    Script Syntax:

    Create ForceModel DefaultProp_ForceModel;
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.CentralBody = Earth;
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.PointMasses = {Sun, Earth, Luna};
Create Propagator DefaultProp;
GMAT DefaultProp.FM = DefaultProp_ForceModel;
GMAT DefaultProp.MinStep = 9.999999999999999e-022;
GMAT DefaultProp.MaxStep = 86400;
GMAT DefaultProp.MaxStepAttempts = 100;

    Figure: DefaultProp Propagator Object

  • Solar System

    • Add a Barycenter under Special Points and rename it DefaultBC

    • Add a Libration Point under Special Points and rename it ESL1

    Script Syntax:

    Create Barycenter DefaultBC;
Create LibrationPoint ESL1;

    Figure: ESL1 Special Point Object

  • Burns

    • Rename DefaultIB to dV

    Script Syntax:

    Create ImpulsiveBurn dV;

  • Variables/Arrays/Strings

    • To create the necessary variables, insert the line of code below into the script just after the setup of the Coordinate System Objects

    Script Syntax:

    Create Variable TotaldV VX VY VZ dVX dVY dVZ I;

  • Coordinate Systems

    • EarthSunL1CS

      • Add a new Coordinate System and name it EarthSunL1CS

      • Set the Origin to ESL1

      • Change the Axes type to Object Referenced

      • Change the Primary and Secondary Values to Sun and Earth, respectively

      Script Syntax:

      Create CoordinateSystem EarthSunL1CS;
GMAT EarthSunL1CS.Origin = ESL1;
GMAT EarthSunL1CS.Axes = ObjectReferenced;
GMAT EarthSunL1CS.Primary = Sun;
GMAT EarthSunL1CS.Secondary = Earth;

      Figure: EarthSunL1CS Coordinate System Object

    • EarthSunRotCS

      • Add a new Coordinate System and name it EarthSunRotCS

      • Change the Axes type to Object Referenced

      • Change the Primary and Secondary Values to Sun and Earth, respectively

      Script Syntax:

      Create CoordinateSystem EarthSunRotCS;
GMAT EarthSunRotCS.Origin = Earth;
GMAT EarthSunRotCS.Axes = ObjectReferenced;
GMAT EarthSunRotCS.Primary = Sun;

  • Solvers

    • Create a Differential Corrector Object under Solvers > Boundary Value Solvers and name it DefaultDC

    • Add the code lines below to the script under the DefaultDC section

    Script Syntax:

    Create DifferentialCorrector DefaultDC;
GMAT DefaultDC.ShowProgress = true;
GMAT DefaultDC.ReportStyle = Normal;
GMAT DefaultDC.TargeterTextFile = targeter_DefaultDC.data;
GMAT DefaultDC.Variables = {dV.V, dV.N};
GMAT DefaultDC.MaximumIterations = 25;
GMAT DefaultDC.UseCentralDifferences = false;

    Figure: DefaultDC Boundary Value Solver Object

  • Plots/Reports

    • Rename DefaultOpenGL to L1View

    • Create an OpenGL Plot Named EarthSunRotView

      • Set EarthSunL1CS as the both the View Direction and View Up Definition Coordinate System (Note: you will have to create the coordinate system outlined below before taking this step)

      • Change both the View Point Reference and View Direction to ESL1 (Note: again, this will need to be created first)

      • Change the View Scale Factor to 12

      • Uncheck DrawXY Plane and set Solver Iterations to None

      Script Syntax:

      Create OpenGLPlot L1View;
GMAT L1View.SolverIterations = None;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.Add = {ACE, Earth};
GMAT L1View.TargetColor = [ 8421440 0 ];
GMAT L1View.CoordinateSystem = EarthSunL1CS;
GMAT L1View.ViewPointReference = ESL1;
GMAT L1View.ViewDirection = ESL1;
GMAT L1View.ViewScaleFactor = 12;
GMAT L1View.ViewUpCoordinateSystem = EarthSunL1CS;
GMAT L1View.XYPlane = Off;

      Figure: L1View OpenGL Plot Object

    • Create an OpenGL Plot Named EarthSunRotView

      • Add Luna as a Celestial Object and Change its orbit color to Grey

      • Switch both the View Definition and the View Up Direction Coordinate System Objects to EarthSunRotCS (Note: Don't forget to create this System first as well)

      • Set the View Scale Factor to 100

      • Switch the View Up Definition Axis to Y

      • Uncheck DrawXY Plane and set Solver Iterations to None

      Script Syntax:

      Create OpenGLPlot EarthSunRotView;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.SolverIterations = None;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.Add = {ACE, Earth, Luna};
GMAT EarthSunRotView.OrbitColor = [ 255 32768 12632256 ];
GMAT EarthSunRotView.TargetColor = [ 8421440 0 0 ];
GMAT EarthSunRotView.CoordinateSystem = EarthSunRotCS;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.ViewPointVector = [ 0 0 30000 ];
GMAT EarthSunRotView.ViewScaleFactor = 100;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.ViewUpCoordinateSystem = EarthSunRotCS;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.ViewUpAxis = Y;
GMAT EarthSunRotView.XYPlane = Off;

    • Create a Report Named ESL1Ephem

      • Remove all Parameters from the Parameter List

      • Select the File as being ./output/SampleMissions/Ex_ACEStationKeeping.report

      Script Syntax:

      Create ReportFile ESL1Ephem;
GMAT ESL1Ephem.SolverIterations = Current;
GMAT ESL1Ephem.Filename = './output/SampleMissions/Ex_ACEStationKeeping.report';
GMAT ESL1Ephem.Precision = 16;
GMAT ESL1Ephem.WriteHeaders = On;
GMAT ESL1Ephem.LeftJustify = On;
GMAT ESL1Ephem.ZeroFill = Off;
GMAT ESL1Ephem.ColumnWidth = 20;

Creating and Configuring the Mission Sequence

Image of Mission Tree

Now that we have all the resources at out disposal to complete this mission, we will go ahead and start building the mission tree. ACE's mission if fairly straight forward at the level we will be dealing with. As stated before, the primary goal here is to allow the spacecraft seven iterations, or half orbits, and at the beginning of each one, calculate the deltaV required in the perpendicular-to-travel direction required at the ecliptic to ensure no velocity towards or away from the Sun or Earth. Basically, the spacecraft must not have any movement between these two bodies as it passes through the plane on which the Sun and Earth both lie. The entire Mission Sequence is relatively short and is given below in its entirety.

This particular mission tree may be a bit more complex then those you have previously dealt with but it is only due to the several equations and reports that it looks more complicated than it actually is. This part of the tutorial will go through the mission sequence step by step and at the end you will have a functional setup.

  • Delete the initial Propagate

  • Report1:

    • Append this to the Mission Sequence Folder

    • Remove ACE.A1ModJulian from the parameters list

    • Add ACE.EarthSunL1CS.X, Y, Z, VZ, VY, and VZ to the parameters list

  • Equation1: Set to TotaldV = 0

  • For1: Change the End parameter to 7

    • Target1: (Note: In the 6-16-2008 build of GMAT, and for several builds thereafter, the targeter requires an extra parameter. If you are working with a version soon after 6-09-2008, use the line "Target Command DefaultDC {ExitMode = SaveAndContinue};" instead of the normal target line in the script)

      • Vary1

        • Set the variable to dV.B

        • Set the initial value to 0

        • Set the perturbation to 1e-5

        • Set the Lower to -0.1

        • Set the Upper to 0.1

        • Set the Max Step to 0.01

      • Equation2: Set as VX = ACE.VX

      • Equation3: Set as VY = ACE.VY

      • Equation4: Set as VZ = ACE.VZ

      • Maneuver1

      • Equation5: Set as ACE.VX - VX

      • Equation6: Set as ACE.VY - VY

      • Equation7: Set as ACE.VZ - VZ

      • Equation8: Set as TotaldV = TotaldV + sqrt( dVZ^2 + dVY^2 + dVZ^2 )

      • Propagate1: Set stopping condition as ACE.EarthSunL1CS.Y = 0

      • Achieve1: Set the goal as ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VX = 0 with a tolerance of 1e-005

    • Propagate2

    • Report2

      • Remove ACE.A1ModJulian and put in ACE.UTCGregorian

      • Add ACE.EarthSunL1CS.X, Y, Z, VZ, VY, and VZ to the parameters list

Script Syntax:

Report ESL1Ephem ACE.EarthSunL1CS.X ACE.EarthSunL1CS.Y ACE.EarthSunL1CS.Z ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VX ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VY ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VZ

GMAT TotaldV = 0;
For I = 1:7 

   Target DefaultDC;

      Vary DefaultDC(dV.B = 0, {Perturbation = 1e-5, MaxStep = 0.01, Lower = -0.1, Upper = 0.1});

      GMAT VX = ACE.VX;
      GMAT VY = ACE.VY;
      GMAT VZ = ACE.VZ;

      Maneuver dV(ACE);

      GMAT dVX = ACE.VX - VX;
      GMAT dVY = ACE.VY - VY; 
      GMAT dVZ = ACE.VZ - VZ;

      GMAT TotaldV = TotaldV + sqrt(  dVZ^2 + dVY^2 + dVZ^2  );    

      Propagate DefaultProp(ACE, {ACE.EarthSunL1CS.Y = 0});

      Achieve DefaultDC(ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VX = 0, {Tolerance = 1e-005});

   EndTarget;  % For targeter DefaultDC
   Propagate DefaultProp(ACE);

   Report ESL1Ephem ACE.UTCGregorian ACE.EarthSunL1CS.X ACE.EarthSunL1CS.Y ACE.EarthSunL1CS.Z ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VX ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VY ACE.EarthSunL1CS.VZ

EndFor;

Figure: Equation1 Equation Command

Figure: Report1 Report Command

Figure: For1 For Command

Figure: Target1 Target Command Command

Figure: Vary1 Vary Command

Figure: Maneuver1 Maneuver Command

Figure: Propagate1 Propagate Command

Figure: Achieve1 Achieve Command Command

Running the Mission

Image of Output Tree

While running this setup, you should see the spacecraft ACE make seven half-loops around the Sun-Earth L1 Libration Point. Just before each run you will see a slight pause in drawing of the model as GMAT computes the needed change in velocity. As you may be able to see in the reports, the changes in velocity here are quite small due to this Libration Point's unstable nature.

If you look into the reports stored in the directory specified then you will find the various parameters that were saved. This information provides insight as to the movement of the ACE spacecraft over time, especially if you take to a more text based presentation of information, rather than a visual one.

By now you should understand not only how to setup the required objects for this mission such as the Barycenter, Libration Point, Coordinate System Objects, Reports, Variable Object, and different views for the OpenGL Plot Object, but also how to apply these to create an effective and well documented mission. Below are the screen captures of both the output tree (where you can view the report output information) and the output window itself.

Figure: Output

Chapter 19. Lunar Transfer

Table of Contents

Objective and Overview
Prerequisites
Mission Description
Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Creating and Modifying Sequences
Running the Mission

This tutorial was started from the default settings in the June 9, 2008 build of GMAT.

Objective and Overview

The primary goal of this mission is for you to learn how to create and propagate a transfer trajectory from a LEO (Low Earth Orbit) to a lunar orbit. Given the capabilities of GMAT, you will also learn how to solve for several initially unknown variables and apply them to give your spacecraft a more efficient path to the moon.

Download the script file: LunarTransferTutorial.script

Prerequisites

  • Basic understanding of Hohmann Transfer trajectories

  • Tutorials:

    • Creating and Propagating a Spacecraft

    • Designing a Hohmann Transfer

Mission Description

  • Objective: Target a lunar transfer trajectory with several initially undetermined variables and achieve a given altitude for a lunar propagation.

  • Assume:

    • Launch site is Kennedy Space Center (INC = 28.5°)

    • Parking orbit altitude is 185 km (SMA = 6555 km)

    • Parking orbit is nearly circular (ECC = 0.001)

  • Find:

    • RAAN

    • AOP

    • ΔV

Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Figure: Lunar Transfer Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree

For this tutorial, two spacecraft, two impulsive burns, and three undetermined variables are needed in order to propagate a viable lunar transfer trajectory to a lunar orbit. To realistically account for the varying gravitational fields of the sun, earth, and moon, three propagators are required. Two OpenGL plots are needed to see how the spacecraft and its trajectory would look from an arbitrary point of view in space. Finally, an earth-lunar and lunar coordinate system should be used to allow for an easier interpretation of how the spacecraft is positioned once the moon is the primary body of its propagation.

Objects Required

  • Spacecraft: InitSat and Sat

  • Impulsive Burns: TOI (Transfer Orbit Insertion) and LOI (Lunar Orbit Insertion)

  • Propagators: EarthOnlyProp, NearEarthProp, and NearMoonProp

  • Plots/Reports: EarthOGL and EarthMoonOGL

  • Variables/Arrays/Strings: RAAN, AOP, and ΔV

  • Coordinate Systems: EarthToMoon and LunaFixed

Creating and Modifying Objects

  • Spacecraft

    • Add a spacecraft to the resource tree and name it Sat

    • Set the epoch format to UTCGregorian

    • Use Keplerian as the State Type for the coordinate system

    • See Assumptions to modify spacecraft element properties

    • Clone Sat and rename it InitSat

    Script Syntax:

    Create Spacecraft Sat;
GMAT Sat.DateFormat = UTCGregorian;
GMAT Sat.DisplayStateType = Keplerian;
GMAT Sat.SMA = 6554.999999999999;
GMAT Sat.ECC = 0.0009999999999997056;
GMAT Sat.INC = 28.50000000000001;
Create Spacecraft InitSat;

    Figure: Sat Spacecraft Object

  • Propagators

    • EarthOnly:

      • Include only a heliocentric pointmass

      Script Syntax:

      Create ForceModel EarthOnly_ForceModel;
GMAT EarthOnly_ForceModel.PointMasses = {Sun};

Create Propagator EarthOnly;

      Figure: NearEarthProp Propagator Object

    • NearEarthProp:

      • Include heliocentric and lunar point masses

      Script Syntax:

      Create ForceModel NearEarthProp_ForceModel;
GMAT NearEarthProp_ForceModel.PointMasses = {Sun, Luna};

Create Propagator NearEarthProp;
GMAT NearEarthProp.FM = NearEarthProp_ForceModel;

    • NearMoonProp:

      • Use the moon as the only Primary Body

      • Change the gravity model to LP-165 with a degree and order of 4

      • Include geocentric and heliocentric point masses

      Script Syntax:

      Create ForceModel NearMoonProp_ForceModel;
GMAT NearMoonProp_ForceModel.CentralBody = Luna;
GMAT NearMoonProp_ForceModel.PrimaryBodies = {Luna};
GMAT NearMoonProp_ForceModel.PointMasses = {Sun, Earth};
GMAT NearMoonProp_ForceModel.GravityField.Luna.PotentialFile = 
'LP165P.cof';

Create Propagator NearMoonProp;
GMAT NearMoonProp.FM = NearMoonProp_ForceModel;

  • Burns

    • TOI:

      • Change V to be 2 km/s

      Script Syntax:

      Create ImpulsiveBurn TOI;
GMAT TOI.Element1 = 2;

      Figure: TOI Impulsive Burn Object

    • LOI:

      Script Syntax:

      Create ImpulsiveBurn LOI;

  • Variables/Arrays/Strings

    • Add three variables to the resource tree and name them RAAN, AOP, and ΔV

    • Set each equal to zero and to the Sat spacecraft

    Script Syntax:

    Create Variable RAAN AOP V;

    Figure: RAAN Variable Object

  • Coordinate Systems

    • Add a new system to the resource tree and rename it EarthToMoon

    • Change the origin to be the moon

    • Set the Axes Type to ObjectReferenced

    • Set the moon to be the primary body and the earth to be the secondary body

    Script Syntax:

    Create CoordinateSystem EarthMoonRot;
GMAT EarthMoonRot.Origin = Luna;
GMAT EarthMoonRot.Axes = ObjectReferenced;
GMAT EarthMoonRot.Primary = Luna;
GMAT EarthMoonRot.Secondary = Earth;

    Figure: EarthMoonRot Coordinate System Object

  • Plots/Reports

    • EarthOGL:

      • Add Luna to the Selected Celestial Objects field

      • Use a View Scale Factor of 15

      • Select X as View Up Definition Axis

      Script Syntax:

      Create OpenGLPlot EarthOGL;
GMAT EarthOGL.Add = {Sat, Earth, Luna};
GMAT EarthOGL.ViewScaleFactor = 15;
GMAT EarthOGL.ViewUpAxis = X;

      Figure: EarthOGL OpenGL Plot Object

    • EarthMoonOGL:

      • Add Luna to the Selected Celestial Objects field

      • Change the coordinate system in the View Definition and View Up Definition group boxes to be EarthToMoon

      • Select Luna as the View Point Reference and View Direction body from those drop down menus

      Script Syntax:

      Create OpenGLPlot EarthMoonOGL;
GMAT EarthMoonOGL.Add = {Sat, Luna, Earth};
GMAT EarthMoonOGL.ViewDirection = Luna;
GMAT EarthMoonOGL.ViewUpAxis = Z;
GMAT EarthMoonOGL.ViewPointReference = Earth;
GMAT EarthMoonOGL.CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT EarthMoonOGL.ViewUpCoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;

Creating and Configuring the Mission Sequence

Resource Mission and Output Trees

This mission calls three targeting sequences to accomplish the mission, which are explained below. The goal of the mission is to vary three unknowns, achieve them, and successfully transfer into a lunar, polar, circular orbit. To achieve a polar orbit we will use what is known as B-Plane Targeting to define how we want the orbit to be oriented. Setting the BdotT variable to zero says our spacecraft will orbit over the lunar poles. If the orbit was to be equatorial we would simply replace BdotT with a BdotR of zero. (Note: If the dot product of B and T vectors is unfamiliar to you, Analytical Graphics Inc., makers of STK, has a good website [https://www.analyticalgraphics.com/resources/help/stk613/helpSystem/extfile/gator/eq-bplane.htm|explaining] it).

  • The Target 1 Sequence solves for three specified variables (in this case RAAN, AOP, and ΔV) by appling the first impulsive burn to get the spacecraft to exit its parking orbit and enter a lunar transfer trajectory. The spacecraft is told to propagate from the parking orbit's apoapsis to initiate the sequence.

  • The Target 2 Sequence calls the values achieved in Target 1 to use them as a good initial guess to converge onto a viable lunar transfer trajectory, which is why we needed a second spacecraft. InitSat uses those achieved values and sets them equal to three new Vary commands. These new commands wish to achieve a lunar altitude and BdotT, calling for a definite type of lunar orbit. Also, in order to make things more realistic, two Propagates are added to slowly progress from one dominant gravitational field into another when approaching the moon.

  • The Target 3 Sequence utilizes the second impulsive burn to slow the spacecraft in its velocity direction to achieve a circular eccentricity, and a polar, lunar orbit. This sequence states occurs at lunar apoapsis.

Creating and Modifying Sequences

Target 1 Sequence

  • Target 1:

    • Vary 1:

      • Set the first Variable to Element1 using the TOI impulsive burn

      • Set the Initial Value parameter equal to 3.15 km/s

      • Define the Lower (Limit) to be 3.05 km/s

      • Define the Upper (Limit) to 3.25 km/s

      • Change the Max Step to 0.01 km/s

    • Vary 2:

      • Set the second Variable to AOP

      • Use an Initial Value of 0°

      • Change the Perturbation field to 0.2

      • Change the Max Step to 15°

    • Vary 3:

      • Set the third Variable to RAAN

      • Set the Initial Value equal to 320°

      • Change the Perturbation to 0.2

      • Change the Max Step to 15°

    • Maneuver 1: utilize the TOI impulsive burn

    • Propagate 1: set the Stopping Condition parameter to earth's apoapsis

    • Achieve 1:

      • Goal:

        • Highlight Sat in Object List menu

        • Select the EarthToMoon coordinate system from the drop down menu

        • Add X to the Selected Value(s) field

        • Change the Value field to be 16000 km

    • Achieve 2:

      • Goal:

        • Highlight Sat in Object List menu

        • Select the MarsMJ2000Eq coordinate system from the drop down menu

        • Add Y in to the Selected Value(s) field

        • Change the Value field to be 0 km

    • Achieve 3:

      • Goal:

        • Highlight Sat in Object List menu

        • Select the MarsMJ2000Eq coordinate system from the drop down menu

        • Add Z in to the Selected Value(s) field

        • Change the Value field to be 0 km

Script Syntax:

GMAT InitSat = Sat;
Target DC1;
   Vary DC1(Sat.RAAN = 270, {Perturbation = .01, MaxStep = 15, Lower = -5360, Upper = 5360});
   Vary DC1(Sat.AOP = 0, {Perturbation = .01, MaxStep = 15, Lower = -5360, Upper = 5360});
   Vary DC1(TOI.Element1 = 3.1, {Perturbation = 0.00001, MaxStep = 0.005, Lower = 3.05, Upper = 3.25});
   Maneuver TOI(Sat);
   Propagate EarthOnly(Sat) {Sat.Earth.Apoapsis};
   Achieve DC1(Sat.EarthMoonRot.X = 10000, {Tolerance = 1});
   Achieve DC1(Sat.EarthMoonRot.Y = 0, {Tolerance = 1});
   Achieve DC1(Sat.EarthMoonRot.Z = 0, {Tolerance = 1});
EndTarget;

Figure: Target1 Target Command

Figure: Vary1 Vary Command

Figure: Maneuver1 Maneuver Command

Figure: Propagate1 Propagate Command

Figure: Achieve1 Achieve Command

  • Equation 1: set Sat.RAAN = RAAN

  • Equation 2: set Sat.AOP = AOP

  • Equation 3: set Sat = InitSat

Script Syntax:

GMAT Sat.RAAN = RAAN;
GMAT Sat.AOP = AOP;
GMAT Sat = InitSat;

Figure: Equation1 Equation Command

Target 2 Sequence

  • Target 2:

    • Vary 4:

      • Set the first Variable to Element 1 using TOI impulsive burn

      • Set the Initial Value to TOI.Element1

    • Vary 5:

      • Set the second Variable to AOP

      • Set the Initial Value to AOP

    • Vary 6:

      • Set the third Variable to RAAN

      • Set the Initial Value to RAAN

    • Maneuver 2: utilize the TOI impulsive burn

    • Set the stopping condition parameter to be 2 days for Sat in Propagate 2

    • Set the stopping condition parameter to be lunar periapsis in Propagate 3

    • Achieve 4:

      • Goal:

        • Use Lunar altitude

        • Set the Altitude to 300 km

        • Use a Tolerance of 1.0 km

    • Achieve 5:

      • Define the Goal as BdotT using the EarthToMoon coordinate system

        • Use a BdotT of 0.0 km

        • Use a Tolerance of 1.0 km

Script Syntax:

GMAT Sat = InitSat;
GMAT RAAN = Sat.RAAN;
GMAT AOP = Sat.AOP;

Target DefaultDC;
   Vary DefaultDC(TOI.Element1 = TOI.Element1, {Perturbation = 0.0001, MaxStep = 0.2, Lower = -9.999999e300, Upper = 
      9.999999e300});
   Vary DefaultDC(Sat.AOP = AOP, {Perturbation = 0.1, MaxStep = 15} 

   Vary DefaultDC(Sat.RAAN = RAAN, {Perturbation = 0.1, MaxStep = 15} 
   Maneuver TOI(Sat);
   Propagate EarthMoonProp(Sat) {Sat.ElapsedDays = 2.0};
   Propagate MoonProp(Sat) {Sat.Luna.Periapsis};
   Achieve DefaultDC(Sat.Luna.Altitude = 300, {Tolerance = 1.0});
   Achieve DefaultDC(Sat.EarthToMoon.BdotT = 0.0, {Tolerance = 1.0});
EndTarget;

Target 3 Sequence

  • Target 3:

    • Vary 7:

      • Set the Variable to V using LOI impulsive burn

      • Use an Initial Value of - 0.5 km/s

      • Define the Lower (Limit) to be - 4 km/s

      • Define the (Limit) to be 3.14 km/s

    • Maneuver 3: utilize the LOI impulsive burn

    • Propagate 4: change the Stopping Condition parameter to be lunar apoapsis

    • Achieve 6:

      • Change the Goal to reach a lunar eccentricity

      • Change the eccentricity Value to be equal to zero

Script Syntax:

Target DC1;
   Vary DC1(LOI.Element1 = 0.5, {Perturbation = 0.0001, MaxStep = 0.2, Lower = -4, Upper = 3.14159});
   Maneuver LOI(Sat);
   Propagate NearMoonProp(Sat) {Sat.Luna.Apoapsis};
   Achieve DC1(Sat.Luna.Altitude = 300, {Tolerance = 1});
   Achieve DC1(Sat.Luna.ECC = 0, {Tolerance = 0.1});
EndTarget;
Propagate NearMoonProp(Sat) {Sat.ElapsedDays = 2};
Propagate MoonProp(Sat) {Sat.ElapsedDays = 2.0};

Chapter 20. Formation Rendezvous

This tutorial was started from the default settings in the June 9, 2008 build of GMAT.

Objective and Overview

The primary goal of this mission is for you to learn how to create a formation flying mission that uses targeting sequences. The mission requires spacecraft dependent coordination systems and has plots in different spacecraft dependent coordinate systems and targets variables that are expressed in spacecraft dependent coordinate systems. Also, this mission includes a rendezvous. This tutorial indicates the method in which the spacecraft can accomplish formation flying and formation rendezvous.

Download the script file: FormationRendezvousTutorial.script

Prerequisites

  • Basic Understanding of Formation Rendezvous

Mission Description

  • Objective: Accomplishing a rendezvous by two certain spacecraft from formation flying of four spacecraft.

  • Given:

    • Initial formation states of spacecraft, which indicate orbital elements

  • Find:

    • ?Burn1 (?V, ?N, ?B)

Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Figure: Formation Rendezvous Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree

In this section, some assumptions or conditions are described to accomplish the mission. Four spacecraft are created in this simple mission but only one spacecraft can have its trajectory changed. A single burn and a single propagator are needed as well. Several Plots/Reports and Coordinate Systems are set in order to analyze the details of each spacecraft trajectory.

Objects Required

  • Spacecraft: Sat1, Sat2, Sat3, Sat4

  • Impulsive Burn: Burn1

  • Propagator: RKV_LowEarth

  • Differential Corrector: DC

  • OpenGL Plots: EarthView, DataReport

  • Coordinate systems: Sat1LVLH, Sat2VNB

Creating and Modifying Objects

      • Change the Epoch Format to UTCGregorian

      • Set the Epoch to 01 Jan 2000 11:59:27.966

      • Use Keplerian State Type

      Script Syntax:

      Create Spacecraft Sat1;
GMAT Sat1.Epoch.UTCGregorian = 01 Jan 2000 11:59:27.966;
GMAT Sat1.CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT Sat1.DisplayStateType = Keplerian;
GMAT Sat1.SMA   = 7600;
GMAT Sat1.ECC   = 0;
GMAT Sat1.INC   = 100.51;
GMAT Sat1.AOP  = 0;
GMAT Sat1.RAAN  = 278.85;
GMAT Sat1.TA  = 90;

  • Propagators

Creating and Configuring the Mission Sequence

Image of Output Tree

This mission consists of first sequence, two targeting sequences. The first sequence includes some reports, an equation and a propagator, and the purpose is observation of the achievement of the formation flying under given initial conditions. Each targeting sequence also includes some reports, propagators, an equation and a maneuver, and the goal is the achievement of two formation rendezvous. The details of them are described below.

  • The Target1 Sequence solves for three specified variables (?V, ?N and ?B) by applying Burn1 to Sat2 for accomplishing formation rendezvous which the positions of Sat2 would be same with of Sat1.

  • The Target2 Sequence solves for three specified variables (?V, ?N and ?B) by applying Burn1 to Sat2 for accomplishing formation rendezvous which the velocities of Sat2 would be same with of Sat1.

Creating and Modifying Sequences

First Sequence

  • Toggle1

    • Select Sat1wrtSat2VNB On

  • Toggle2

    • Select Sat2InSat1LVLH On

  • Toggle3

    • Select Sat1wrtSat2VNB2 On

  • Toggle4

    • Select Sat2wrtSat1LVLHOn

  • Report1

    • Add the Cartesian coordinates, X, Y, and Z, and all velocity, VX, VY, and VZ, to the parameters list to report them for Sat1

  • Report2

    • Add the Cartesian coordinates, X, Y, and Z, and all velocity, VX, VY, and VZ, to the parameters list to report them for Sat2

  • Report3

    • Add the Cartesian coordinates, X, Y, and Z, and all velocity, VX, VY, and VZ, to the parameters list to report them for Sat3

  • Report4

    • Add the Cartesian coordinates, X, Y, and Z, and all velocity, VX, VY, and VZ, to the parameters list to report them for Sat4

  • Equation1

    • DataReport.WriteHeaders = Off

  • Propagator1

    • Use RKV_LowEarth propagator

    • Set the stopping condition parameter to 0.2 elapsed days

  • Report5

    • Refer to Report1 for parameters list

  • Report6

    • Refer to Report2 for parameters list

  • Report7

    • Refer to Report3 for parameters list

  • Report8

    • Refer to Report4 for parameters list

Script Syntax:

Toggle Sat1wrtSat2VNB On;
Toggle Sat2InSat1LVLH On;
Toggle Sat1wrtSat2VNB2 On;
Toggle Sat2wrtSat1LVLH On;

Report DataReport Sat1.X Sat1.Y Sat1.Z Sat1.VX Sat1.VY Sat1.VZ;
Report DataReport Sat2.X Sat2.Y Sat2.Z Sat2.VX Sat2.VY Sat2.VZ;
Report DataReport Sat3.X Sat3.Y Sat3.Z Sat3.VX Sat3.VY Sat3.VZ;
Report DataReport Sat4.X Sat4.Y Sat4.Z Sat4.VX Sat4.VY Sat4.VZ;

GMAT DataReport.WriteHeaders = Off;

Propagate RKV_LowEarth(Sat1, Sat2, Sat3, Sat4, {Sat1.ElapsedDays = .2});

Report DataReport Sat1.X Sat1.Y Sat1.Z Sat1.VX Sat1.VY Sat1.VZ;
Report DataReport Sat2.X Sat2.Y Sat2.Z Sat2.VX Sat2.VY Sat2.VZ;
Report DataReport Sat3.X Sat3.Y Sat3.Z Sat3.VX Sat3.VY Sat3.VZ;
Report DataReport Sat4.X Sat4.Y Sat4.Z Sat4.VX Sat4.VY Sat4.VZ;

     Vary DC(Burn1.N = 0.000, {Perturbation = 0.0001, MaxStep = 0.05, Lower = -0.3, Upper = 0.3});

     Achieve DC(Sat2.Sat1LVLH.Y = 0, {Tolerance = 0.0001});

Chapter 21. Minimum Fuel for Orbit Transfer

Table of Contents

Objective and Overview
Prerequisites
Mission Description
Resource, Mission, and Output trees
Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree
Objects Required
Creating and Modifying Objects
Creating and Configuring the Mission Tree
Creating and Modifying Command Sequences
Running the Mission

This tutorial was started from the default settings in the July 2, 2008 build of GMAT.

Objective and Overview

This tutorial shows how GMAT's optimizer can be used in a mission setting. This mission basically shows how a Hohmann transfer is the most efficient to go from one orbit to the other. While this isn't entirely a Hohmann transfer since it also has a plane change, it generally abides by its rules. Again, this tutorial will show how the optimize, optimizer, vary command using the optimizer, nonlinear constraints, and minimize command. To accomplish this, the transfer orbit insertion burn and the final orbit insertion burn will each vary in all directions. Additionally, the time that the spacecraft flies in the transfer orbit and the time/point that it leaves the initial orbit are both varied as well.

Download the script file: Ex_LowEarthMinFuelTransfer.script

Note: This mission is the same as the Optimization sample mission largely, except the Optimization mission has a few errors in it and does not contain XY Plots

Prerequisites

Mission Description

  • Objective:

    • SMA=10,000

    • ECC=.05

    • INC=5

    • Minimum Fuel Required to Achieve Above Objectives

  • Assume:

    • SMA = 7500

    • ECC = 0

    • INC = 0

    • RAAN = 45

    • AOP = 0

    • TA = 360

  • Find:

    • Epoch of Transfer Orbit Insertion Burn

    • Epoch of Final Orbit Insertion Burn

    • Transfer Orbit Insertion Burn

    • Final Orbit Insertion Burn

Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Figure: Minimum Fuel Orbit Transfer Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree

Two spacecraft will be required, one for actual propagation and the other is a dummy satellite whose conditions we don't care about but For this mission, two burns will be required. One burn will transfer the spacecraft from its initial orbit to its transfer orbit. The second burn will transfer the spacecraft from its transfer orbit to its final orbit. Only one propagator is needed since the spacecraft is staying close to Earth. Only one OpenGL plot will be used. One report file will be used to store the final numbers of the burns and to see how closely it achieves the desired goals. Four XY plots will be used to observe how quickly convergence is achieved for the objectives of the mission. Also an optimizer will be used instead of a differential corrector. Also a number of variables will be used.

Objects Required

  • Spacecraft: Sat, DummySat

  • Burns: dV1, dV2

  • Propagators: DefaultProp

  • Optimizer: SPQfmincon

  • Plots/Reports: DefaultOpenGL, IterateData, CostPlot, SMAPlot, ECCPlot, INCPlot

  • Coordinate Systems:EarthMJ2000Eq

  • Variables: TOF dV1Time Cost Constraint1 Constraint2 Constraint3, dV1mag dV2mag RefEpoch PropEpoch Iterate

  • Propagators

    • DefaultProp

      • It uses all of the default values except it has no primary body, but rather uses a point force model of the Earth with no drag. If it was desired to make it more accurate, drag, J2, solar radiation, and other celestial bodies could be added to the propagator.

      Script Syntax:

      Create ForceModel DefaultProp_ForceModel;
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.CentralBody = Earth;
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.PointMasses = {Earth};
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.Drag = None;
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.SRP = Off;
GMAT DefaultProp_ForceModel.ErrorControl = RSSStep;

Create Propagator DefaultProp;

      Figure: DefaultProp Propagator Object

Creating and Configuring the Mission Tree

Resource Mission and Output Trees

The spacecraft propagates a single orbit and then the optimizing sequence starts. First the time of the transfer orbit insertion burn is varied to determine the best time to start the orbit insertion. The two if statements depend on if the time is negative or positive. If it is positive, the first if statement allows the spacecraft to propagate forward in time to that point. If it is negative, the second if statement allows the spacecraft to propagate backwards in time to that point. Next the three directions of the first burn are varied in magniture. Then the maneuever is performed and the amount of time the spacecraft is on that transfer orbit is varied. Then the magnitude of the three directions of the second transfer burn

Creating and Modifying Command Sequences

Pre-Optimization Sequence

  • Firstly, the four XY plots are turned off so that they can only take data when we want them to be. If they were left on, they would take the wrong data. We want them to take a measurement at the end of the iteration so we know how close each iteration is to the final value.

  • The propagate command is then to make the spacecraft orbit one period so that we can see what the original orbit looked like.

  • In Equation2, the counter variable is set to 0 before the optimization sequence starts.

  • Toggle CostPlot Off;

  • Toggle SMAPlot Off;

  • Toggle ECCPlot Off;

  • Toggle INCPlot Off;

  • Propagate Sat for Elapsed Seconds = Sat . Period

  • Equation1 RefEpoch = Sat.A1ModJulian

  • Equation2 Iterate = 0

Script Syntax:

Toggle CostPlot Off;
Toggle SMAPlot Off;
Toggle ECCPlot Off;
Toggle INCPlot Off;
Propagate DefaultProp(Sat) {Sat.ElapsedSecs = Sat.OrbitPeriod};
GMAT RefEpoch = Sat.A1ModJulian;
GMAT Iterate = 0;

Figure: Toggle1 Command

Figure: Propagate Command

Figure: Equation1 Command

Optimization Sequence - Part 1

  • Equation3 counts the number of iterations performed in the optimization sequence. This number will allow tracking of the data in regards to the particular iteration. This is helpful for the ReportFile and the XY Plots.

  • The time when the transfer orbit insertion burn is started is varied. Note that the units on dV1Time(as well as A1ModJulian) is days.

  • Equation4 is used to change the point to which it propagates to.

  • The first If statement allows it to propagate forward while the second If statement allows it to propagate backwards, thus covering the entire orbit so that a burn is possible at any point.

  • Equation3 Iterate = Iterate + 1

  • Vary dV1 Time

    • Lower = -.5, Upper = .5, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 10

  • Equation4 PropEpoch = RefEpoch + dV1Time

  • If dV1 > 0

    • Propagate until Sat.A1ModJulian = PropEpoch

  • If dV1 < 0

    • Backwards Propagate until Sat.A1ModJulian = PropEpoch

Script Syntax:

Vary SQPfmincon(dV1Time = 0.1, {Lower = -.5, Upper = 0.5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0.0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 10});
   GMAT PropEpoch = RefEpoch + dV1Time;
   If dV1Time > 0
      Propagate DefaultProp(Sat) {Sat.A1ModJulian = PropEpoch};
   EndIf;
   If dV1Time < 0
      Propagate BackProp DefaultProp(Sat) {Sat.A1ModJulian = PropEpoch};
   EndIf;

Figure: Vary1 Command

Figure: If Command

Optimization Sequence - Part 2

  • First the transfer orbit insertion burn is varied and the maneuver is applied.

  • Next the time in which it remains in the transfer orbit (TOF) is varied.

  • Now TOF is summed with RefEpoch so that Sat is propagated to the correct location.

  • Final orbit insertion burn is varied and the maneuver is applied.

  • The final values for the SMA, ECC, and INC are stored in variables. The reason SMA is divided by 10000 is to give it a wider tolerance.

  • The goal values for SMA, ECC, and INC are compared to the goal values by using Nonlinear Constraints.

  • Equation10 and 11 are used to find the magnitude of the burns.

  • It is then made so that the value to be minimized is the Cost

  • A ScriptEvent is inserted in the mission sequence for simplicity

    • The four XY plots are turned on so that they are able to record data.

    • The DummySat is propagated a step. In order for any data to be recorded by an XY plot, a propagation of any sort needs to take place, thus a DummySat is used which is not useful or needed beyond this particular need.

    • The four XY plots are turned off, so that they will not record the other values that aren't useful.

  • Thus the Optimization Sequence Closes

  • Vary2: dv1.V

    • Initial = .1, Lower = -5, Upper = 5

  • Vary3: dv1.N

    • Initial = .01, Lower = -5, Upper = 5

  • Vary4: dv1.B

    • Initial = .01, Lower = -5, Upper = 5

  • Maneuver1: Apply dv1 to Sat

  • Vary5: TOF

    • Initial = .3, Lower = 0, Upper = 1, Multiplicative Scale Factor= 10

  • Equation5: PropEpoch = RefEpoch + TOF

  • Propagate4: Sat until Sat.A1ModJulian = PropEpoch

  • Vary6: dv2.V

    • Initial = .1, Lower = -5, Upper = 5

  • Vary7: dv2.N

    • Initial = .01, Lower = -5, Upper = 5

  • Vary8: dv2.B

    • Initial = .01, Lower = -5, Upper = 5

  • Maneuver2: Apply dv2 to Sat

  • Equation6: Constraint1 = Sat.SMA/10000

  • Equation7: Constraint2 = Sat.ECC

  • Equation8: Constraint3 = Sat.INC

  • Nonlinear Constraint1 : Constraint1 = 1

  • Nonlinear Constraint2 : Constraint2 = .05

  • Nonlinear Constraint3 : Constraint3 = 5

  • Equation9: dV1mag = sqrt( dv1.Element1^2 + dv1.Element2^2 + dv1.Element3^2 )

  • Equation10: dV2mag = sqrt( dv2.Element1^2 + dv2.Element2^2 + dv2.Element3^2 )

  • Equation11: Cost = ( dV1mag + dV2mag )

  • Minimize1: Cost

  • Script Event

    • Report IterateData dV1Time TOF Cost Sat.SMA Sat.ECC Sat.INC;

    • Toggle CostPlot On;

    • Toggle SMAPlot On;

    • Toggle ECCPlot On;

    • Toggle INCPlot On;

    • Propagate DefaultProp(DummySat);

    • Toggle CostPlot Off;

    • Toggle SMAPlot Off;

    • Toggle ECCPlot Off;

    • Toggle INCPlot Off;

Script Syntax:

Vary SQPfmincon(dv1.Element1 = 0.1, {Lower = -5, Upper = 5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
   Vary SQPfmincon(dv1.Element2 = 0.01, {Lower = -5, Upper = 5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
   Vary SQPfmincon(dv1.Element3 = 0.01, {Lower = -5, Upper = 5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
   Maneuver dv1(Sat);

   Vary SQPfmincon(TOF = 0.3, {Lower = 0, Upper = 1, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0.0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 10});
   GMAT PropEpoch = RefEpoch + TOF;
   Propagate DefaultProp(Sat) {Sat.A1ModJulian = PropEpoch};
   
   Vary SQPfmincon(dv2.Element1 = 0.1, {Lower = -5, Upper = 5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
   Vary SQPfmincon(dv2.Element2 = 0.01, {Lower = -5, Upper = 5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
   Vary SQPfmincon(dv2.Element3 = 0.01, {Lower = -5, Upper = 5, AdditiveScaleFactor = 0, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
   Maneuver dv2(Sat);
   
   GMAT Constraint1 = Sat.SMA/10000;
   GMAT Constraint2 = Sat.ECC;
   GMAT Constraint3 = Sat.INC;

   NonlinearConstraint SQPfmincon(Constraint1=1);    % SMA Constraint
   NonlinearConstraint SQPfmincon(Constraint2=0.05);    % ECC Constraint 
   NonlinearConstraint SQPfmincon(Constraint3=5);    % INC Constraint
   
   GMAT dV1mag = sqrt( dv1.Element1^2 + dv1.Element2^2 + dv1.Element3^2 );
   GMAT dV2mag = sqrt( dv2.Element1^2 + dv2.Element2^2 + dv2.Element3^2 );
   GMAT Cost = ( dV1mag + dV2mag );
   Minimize SQPfmincon(Cost);

   BeginScript
      Report IterateData dV1Time TOF Cost Sat.SMA Sat.ECC Sat.INC;
      Toggle CostPlot On;
      Toggle SMAPlot On;
      Toggle ECCPlot On;
      Toggle INCPlot On;
      Propagate DefaultProp(DummySat);
      Toggle CostPlot Off;
      Toggle SMAPlot Off;
      Toggle ECCPlot Off;
      Toggle INCPlot Off;
   EndScript;

EndOptimize;  % For optimizer SQPfmincon

Figure: Maneuver Command

Figure: Nonlinear Constraint Command

Figure: Minimize Command

Figure: ScriptEvent Command

Closing Sequence

  • SolutionData is reported to IterateData

  • TOF and Cost is reported to IterateData

  • Sat.SMA, Sat.ECC, Sat.INC are reported to IterateData

  • dv1.V, dv1.N, dv1.B are reported to IterateData

  • dv2.V, dv2.N, dv2.B are reported to IterateData

  • Sat is propagated for one orbital period

Script Syntax:

Report IterateData SolutionData;
Report IterateData TOF Cost;
Report IterateData Sat.SMA Sat.ECC Sat.INC;
Report IterateData dv1.Element1 dv1.Element2 dv1.Element3;
Report IterateData dv2.Element1 dv2.Element2 dv2.Element3;

Propagate DefaultProp(Sat) {Sat.ElapsedSecs = Sat.OrbitPeriod};

Running the Mission

Resource Mission and Output Trees

The SMAPlot should have a large spike but be largely constant otherwise at about 10000. The INC plot starts increasing then decreasing, is constant for a time, spikes, and then is largely constant at about 5 degrees. The ECC plot is largely zeroed except for a single spike. The Cost plot decreases by a small amount, spikes, and then is constants largely at some value near 1.

Figure: Output

Figure: GL plot enlarged Command

Chapter 22. Minimum Fuel for Lunar Transfer

Running the Mission

This tutorial was started from the default settings in the July 2, 2008 build of GMAT.

Objective and Overview

This mission demonstrates further use of optimization sequences. This optimization sequence minimizes the amount of fuel from the Earth to the moon using a standard two-burn trajectory to the moon. Note that this is not a low energy boundary orbit.

Download the script file: Ex_MinFuelLunarCapture.script

Prerequisites

Mission Description

  • Objective:

    • Minimal Fuel Requirements to go from LEO to Orbit about Moon

    • Luna.SMA = 7600

    • Luna.ECC = 0.2

    • MoonMJ2000Eq.INC = 85

  • Assume:

    • Epoch.UTCGregorian = 22 Jul 2014 11:29:10.811;

    • Using the CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;

      • X = -137380.19843385062;

      • Y = 75679.878675370544;

      • Z = 21487.638751878556;

      • VX = -0.23245320142355028;

      • VY = -0.44627539677580192;

      • VZ = 0.085612056628771024;

      • DryMass = 1000;

      • Cd = 2.2000000000000002;

      • Cr = 1.7;

      • DragArea = 15;

      • SRPArea = 1;

  • Find:

    • Minimum burn requirements for Transfer Orbit Insertion

    • Minimum burn requirements for Lunar Orbit Insertion

GMAT OGL_EarthMJ2K.UpdatePlotFrequency = 50;
GMAT OGL_EarthMJ2K.NumPointsToRedraw = 150;
GMAT OGL_EarthMJ2K.UseInitialView = On;

Create OpenGLPlot OGL_MoonMJ2K;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.Add = {MMSRef, Earth, Luna};
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.CoordinateSystem = MoonMJ2000Eq;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.ViewPointReference = Luna;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.ViewDirection = Luna;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.ViewScaleFactor = 1;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.FixedFovAngle = 45;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.ViewUpCoordinateSystem = MoonMJ2000Eq;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.ViewUpAxis = X;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.CelestialPlane = Off;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.XYPlane = On;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.WireFrame = Off;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.SolverIterations = All;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.Axes = On;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.SunLine = Off;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.PerspectiveMode = Off;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.UseFixedFov = Off;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.DataCollectFrequency = 5;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.UpdatePlotFrequency = 50;
GMAT OGL_MoonMJ2K.NumPointsToRedraw = 75;

    Figure: OGL_EarthMJ2K Open GLPlot Object

    • XYPlot LunarINC

      • X: Iteration

      • Y: MoonMJ2000Eq.INC

    • XYPlot LunarSMA

      • X: Iteration

      • Y: Luna.SMA

    • XYPlot LunarECC

      • X: Iteration

      • Y: Luna.ECC

    • XYPlot TotaldVPlot

      • X: Iteration

      • Y: TotaldV

    Script Syntax:

    Create XYPlot LunarINC
GMAT LunarINC.IndVar = Iteration;
GMAT LunarINC.Add    = { MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.INC };
GMAT LunarINC.Grid 	 = On;
GMAT LunarINC.SolverIterations = All;

Create XYPlot LunarSMA
GMAT LunarSMA.IndVar = Iteration;
GMAT LunarSMA.Add    = { MMSRef.Luna.SMA };
GMAT LunarSMA.Grid   = On;
GMAT LunarSMA.SolverIterations = All;

Create XYPlot LunarECC
GMAT  LunarECC.IndVar = Iteration;
GMAT LunarECC.Add     = { MMSRef.Luna.ECC };
GMAT LunarECC.Grid    = On;
GMAT LunarECC.SolverIterations = All;

Create XYPlot TotaldVPlot;
TotaldVPlot.IndVar = Iteration;
TotaldVPlot.Add    = TotaldV;
TotaldVPlot.SolverIterations = All;

    Figure: LunarINC XY Plot Object

    • ReportFile IterateData

      • Filename: ./output/SampleMissions/Ex_MinFuelLunarCapture.report

    Script Syntax:

    Create ReportFile IterateData;
IterateData.Filename = ./output/SampleMissions/Ex_MinFuelLunarCapture.report;

    Figure: IterateData FileReport Object

Creating and Configuring the Mission Tree

Resource Mmission and Output Trees

This mission is set-up very similarly to how the Lunar Transfer Tutorial is set-up, except that optimization sequences are used instead of targeting sequences.

  • Optimization Sequence Setup

    • Turn off the plots until the proper moment to record data and propagate spacecraft until periapsis

  • Optimization Sequence and Final Commands

    • Vary LSI in all directions, perform the burn and propagate to Lunar periapsis, period of time, or until it exits region of space.

    • Nonlinear Constraints on BdotT, BdotR, and Luna.RMag to constrain how far from the moon it can go

    • Vary LOI in all directions and perform burn

    • Nonlinear Constraints dictating goals of mission

    • Propagate for period of time or until it exits region of space

    • Create Equations to find the magnitude of the burns and take the sum of the two burns

    • Minimize the Total amount of dV required by the two burns

    • Toggle on plots to record data, propagate dummy spacecraft for data to be recorded, toggle off plots

    • Report Parameters to report file

Creating and Modifying Command Sequences

Optimization Sequence Setup

  • Toggle off LunarINC, LunarSMA, LunarECC, and TotaldVPlot

  • Propagate MMSRef til Periapsis using LunarSB propagator

  • Equation1: Iteration = 0

Script Syntax:

Toggle LunarINC Off; 
Toggle LunarSMA Off; 
Toggle LunarECC Off;
Toggle TotaldVPlot Off;
Propagate LunarSB(MMSRef, {MMSRef.Periapsis});
Iteration = 0;

Figure: Toggle Command

Figure: Propagate Command

Figure: Equation1 Command

Optimization Sequence and Final Commands

  • Equation2: Iteration = Iteration + 1

  • Vary LSI.V

    • Initial Guess = .1462, Lower = -1, Upper = 1

  • Vary LSI.N

    • Initial Guess = .0460, Lower = -1, Upper = 1

  • Vary LSI.B

    • Initial Guess = .1086, Lower = -1, Upper = 1

  • Maneuver MMSRef using LSI

  • Propagate MMSRef til for 1.5 days using LunarSB propagator

  • Propagate MMSRef using MoonCentered propagator til: Luna Periapsis, 8 days have elapsed, Luna.RMAG = 1000, Earth.RMAG = 3000.

  • Nonlinear Constraint: MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.BdotT <= 20000.0

  • NonlinearConstraint: MMSRef.Luna.RMAG >= 2000

  • NonlinearConstraint: MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.BdotR <= 15000.0

  • Vary LOI.V

    • Initial Guess = -.752, Lower = -1, Upper = 1

  • Vary LOI.N

    • Initial Guess = 0, Lower = -1, Upper = 1

  • Vary LOI.B

    • Initial Guess = 0, Lower = -1, Upper = 1

  • Maneuver MMSRef using LOI

  • NonlinearConstraint: MMSRef.Luna.SMA = 7600

  • NonlinearConstraint: MMSRef.Luna.ECC = 0.2

  • NonlinearConstraint: MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.INC = 85

  • Propagate MMSRef using MoonCentered propagator til: Luna.Periapsis, 5 days have elapsed, Luna.RMAG = 1000, Earth.RMAG = 3000

  • Equation3: dV1Mag = sqrt( LSI.Element1^2 + LSI.Element2^2 + LSI.Element3^2 )

  • Equation4: dV2Mag = sqrt( LOI.Element1^2 + LOI.Element2^2 + LOI.Element3^2 )

  • Equation5: TotaldV = ( dV1Mag + dV2Mag )

  • Minimize TotaldV

  • Report to IterateData: TotaldV, Luna.SMA, Luna.ECC, MoonMJ2000Eq.INC

  • Toggle On LunarINC, LunarSMA, LunarECC, TotaldVPlot

  • Propagate DummySat using LunarSB

  • Toggle Off LunarINC, LunarSMA, LunarECC, TotaldVPlot

  • End Optimization Sequence

  • Report to IterateData: TotaldV, dV1Mag, dV2Mag, MMSRef.Luna.SMA, MMSRef.Luna.ECC MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.INC, LSI.Element1, LSI.Element2, LSI.Element3, LOI.Element1, LOI.Element2 LOI.Element3

  • Propagate MMSRef using MoonCentered propagator for 15 days

Script Syntax:

Optimize SQP1

     Iteration = Iteration + 1;

     Vary SQP1(LSI.V = 0.1462 ,   { Lower = -1, Upper = 1, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
     Vary SQP1(LSI.N = 0.0460 ,   { Lower = -1, Upper = 1, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
     Vary SQP1(LSI.B = 0.1086 ,   { Lower = -1, Upper = 1, MultiplicativeScaleFactor = 1});
     Maneuver LSI(MMSRef);
     
     Propagate LunarSB(MMSRef, {MMSRef.ElapsedDays = 1.5});
     Propagate MoonCentered(MMSRef, {MMSRef.Luna.Periapsis, MMSRef.ElapsedDays = 8, MMSRef.Luna.RMAG = 1000, MMSRef.Earth.RMAG = 3000});

     NonlinearConstraint SQP1(MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.BdotT <= 20000.0); 
     NonlinearConstraint SQP1(MMSRef.Luna.RMAG >= 2000);
     NonlinearConstraint SQP1(MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.BdotR <= 15000.0); 

     Vary SQP1(LOI.V = -0.75198120104, { Lower = -1, Upper = 1});
     Vary SQP1(LOI.N = 0, {  Lower = -1, Upper = 1});
     Vary SQP1(LOI.B = 0, { Lower = -1, Upper = 1});
     Maneuver LOI(MMSRef); 

     NonlinearConstraint SQP1(MMSRef.Luna.SMA = 7600);   
     NonlinearConstraint SQP1(MMSRef.Luna.ECC = 0.2);  
     NonlinearConstraint SQP1(MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.INC = 85);   

     Propagate MoonCentered(MMSRef, {MMSRef.Luna.Periapsis, MMSRef.ElapsedDays = 5, MMSRef.Luna.RMAG = 1000, MMSRef.Earth.RMAG = 3000}); 
     
     dV1Mag = sqrt( LSI.Element1^2 + LSI.Element2^2 + LSI.Element3^2 );
     dV2Mag = sqrt( LOI.Element1^2 + LOI.Element2^2 + LOI.Element3^2 ); 
     TotaldV = ( dV1Mag + dV2Mag );
     Minimize SQP1(TotaldV);

     Report IterateData TotaldV  MMSRef.Luna.SMA MMSRef.Luna.ECC MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.INC;

     Toggle LunarINC On; 
     Toggle LunarSMA On; 
     Toggle LunarECC On;
     Toggle TotaldVPlot On;
     Propagate LunarSB(DummySat);
     Toggle LunarINC Off; 
     Toggle LunarSMA Off; 
     Toggle LunarECC Off;
     Toggle TotaldVPlot Off;

EndOptimize

Report IterateData TotaldV dV1Mag dV2Mag 
Report IterateData MMSRef.Luna.SMA MMSRef.Luna.ECC MMSRef.MoonMJ2000Eq.INC;
Report IterateData LSI.Element1 LSI.Element2 LSI.Element3
Report IterateData LOI.Element1 LOI.Element2 LOI.Element3

Propagate MoonCentered(MMSRef, {MMSRef.ElapsedDays = 15});

Figure: Vary Command

Figure: Maneuver Command

Figure: Nonlinear Constant Command

Figure: Minimize Command

Figure: Report Command

Running the Mission

Resource Mission and Output Trees

The XY plots should look like the ones observed in the screenshot. Notice that the SMA, INC, and ECC plots converge upon the desired values. Additionally, notice how the TotaldVPlot decreases as time goes on. The values that are lower in this plot, on the left side, are iterations that did not complete the required objectives. The Moon plot should show multiple iterations eventually converging upon an iteration that circles the moon. The Earth plot shows a straight line from the Earth to the path of the moon, where you can see the spacecraft follow a sinusoidal shape along the moon's path. This shows the spacecraft orbiting the moon. The spacecraft does not travel in a straight line, this is due to a mistake in the programming of when the plot is on.

Figure: Output

Chapter 23. LEO Station Keeping

Table of Contents

Objective and Overview
Prerequisites
Mission Description
Resource, Mission, and Output trees
Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree
Objects Required
Creating and Modifying Objects
Creating and Configuring the Mission Sequence
Running the Mission

This tutorial was started from the default settings in the June 9, 2008 build of GMAT.

Objective and Overview

This basic tutorial explains how to perform basic station keeping of a spacecraft's semi-major axis and right ascension of the ascending node while in low Earth orbit. The strategy used here to keep the spacecraft in its orbit is somewhat crude compared to that used by actual spacecraft. However, this information is still valuable in that it provides a good example for using control logic and targeting sequences in the same mission.

Download the script file: LEOStationKeepingTutorial.script

Prerequisites

  • Knowledge

    • Basic understanding of Keplarian orbital parameters

    • Basic understanding of low Earth orbit station keeping

  • Tutorials:

    • Creaitng and Propagating a Spacecraft

    • Designing a Hohmann Transfer

  • Objects:

    • Spacecraft Object-Orbit Tab

    • Impulsive Burn Object

    • Propagator Object

    • Differential Corrector Object

    • OpenGL Plot Object

    • Coordinate System Objects

  • Commands:

    • While Command

    • If

    • Maneuver Command

    • Propagate Command

Mission Description

  • Objective

    • Maintain a low Earth orbit by making corrections to the spacecraft's altitude and right ascension of the ascending node.

  • Assume:

    • A spacecraft in a preexisting orbit with a given epoch and orbital parameters

    • A realistic force model including non-spherical gravity and atmospheric drag

  • Find:

    • The deltaV required in the spacecraft's direction of travel to keep it in orbit within the given altitude

    • The deltaV required perpendicular to the spacecraft's direction of travel to keep its right ascension of the ascending node from drifting with respect to the inertial frame

Resource, Mission, and Output trees

Figure: The Resource, Mission, and Output trees for this particular LEO station keeping mission

Creating and Configuring the Resource Tree

This section will outline exactly what resources are required to complete the mission outlined within this tutorial. The spacecraft Sat will be in a highly inclined orbit of nearly 97 degrees. As stated previously, these resources will give you the tools necessary to keep LEOsat in its orbit.

Objects Required

  • Spacecraft: LEOsat

  • Burns: DefaultIB (default)

  • Propagators: LEOprop

  • Solvers: DC1

  • Plots/Reports: SMAview , RAANview

Creating and Modifying Objects

  • Spacecraft

    • Rename DefaultSC to LEOsat

    • Change the Epoch Format to UTCGregorian

    • Set the Epoch to Jan 01 2000 11:59:28.000

    • Switch the State Type to Keplarian

    • Set SMA = 6738.95113401 , ECC = 0.00168481942805 , INC = 96.8535019521 , RAAN = 279.829547746 , AOP = 246.130924803 , TA = 308.589822969

    • Note that when you click 'Apply' in this window, some of the values for your orbital elements may change but this is normal and does not require you to change them back again

    Script Syntax:

    Create Spacecraft LEOsat;
GMAT LEOsat.DateFormat = UTCGregorian;
GMAT LEOsat.Epoch = '01 Jan 2000 11:59:28.000';
GMAT LEOsat.CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT LEOsat.DisplayStateType = Keplerian;
GMAT LEOsat.SMA = 6738.95113401;
GMAT LEOsat.ECC = 0.001684819428049389;
GMAT LEOsat.INC = 96.8535019521;
GMAT LEOsat.RAAN = 279.829547746;
GMAT LEOsat.AOP = 246.1309248029877;
GMAT LEOsat.TA = 308.5898229690123;

    Figure: LEOsat Spacecraft Object

  • Propagators

    • Rename DefaultProp to LEOprop

    • Change both the Degree and Order of the gravity model to 10 to make it more realistic

    • Set the Atmosphere Model to JacchiaRoberts

    • Add the Sun, and Luna as Point Masses

    • Check the Use Solar Radiation Pressure box

    Script Syntax:

    Create ForceModel LEOprop_ForceModel;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.CentralBody = Earth;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.PrimaryBodies = {Earth};
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.PointMasses = {Sun, Luna};
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.Drag = JacchiaRoberts;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.SRP = On;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.ErrorControl = RSSStep;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.GravityField.Earth.Degree = 10;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.GravityField.Earth.Order = 10;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.GravityField.Earth.PotentialFile = 'JGM2.cof';
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.Drag.F107 = 150;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.Drag.F107A = 150;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.Drag.MagneticIndex = 3;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.SRP.Flux = 1367;
GMAT LEOprop_ForceModel.SRP.Nominal_Sun = 149597870.691;

Create Propagator LEOprop;
GMAT LEOprop.FM = LEOprop_ForceModel;
GMAT LEOprop.Type = RungeKutta89;
GMAT LEOprop.InitialStepSize = 60;
GMAT LEOprop.Accuracy = 9.999999999999999e-012;
GMAT LEOprop.MinStep = 0.001;
GMAT LEOprop.MaxStep = 2700;
GMAT LEOprop.MaxStepAttempts = 50;

    Figure: LEOprop Propagator Object

  • Solvers

    • Create a Differential Corrector Object under Solvers > Boundary Value Solvers

    Script Syntax:

    Create DifferentialCorrector DefaultDC;
GMAT DefaultDC.ShowProgress = true;
GMAT DefaultDC.ReportStyle = Normal;
GMAT DefaultDC.TargeterTextFile = targeter_DefaultDC.data;
GMAT DefaultDC.Variables = {dV.V, dV.N};
GMAT DefaultDC.MaximumIterations = 25;
GMAT DefaultDC.UseCentralDifferences = false;

    Figure: DefaultDC Boundary Value Solver Object

  • Plots/Reports

    • Rename DefaultOpenGL to SMAview

      • Uncheck Draw XY Plane

      • Change the View Point Vector to [ 15000 , 3000 , 0 ]

      Script Syntax:

      Create OpenGLPlot SMAview;
GMAT SMAview.SolverIterations = Current;
GMAT SMAview.Add = {LEOsat, Earth};
GMAT SMAview.OrbitColor = [ 255 32768 ];
GMAT SMAview.TargetColor = [ 8421440 0 ];
GMAT SMAview.CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT SMAview.ViewPointReference = Earth;
GMAT SMAview.ViewPointVector = [ 15000 3000 0 ];
GMAT SMAview.ViewDirection = Earth;
GMAT SMAview.ViewScaleFactor = 1;
GMAT SMAview.ViewUpCoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT SMAview.ViewUpAxis = Z;
GMAT SMAview.XYPlane = Off;

      Figure: L1View OpentGL Plot Object

    • Create an OpenGL Plot named RAANview

      • Add Earth to the Selected Celestial Objects list

      • Uncheck Draw XY Plane

      • Change the View Point Vector to [ 1800 , 0 , 15000 ]

      • Change the View Up Definition Axis to X.

      Script Syntax:

      Create OpenGLPlot RAANview;
GMAT RAANview.SolverIterations = Current;
GMAT RAANview.Add = {LEOsat, Earth};
GMAT RAANview.OrbitColor = [ 255 1743054 ];
GMAT RAANview.TargetColor = [ 8421440 8421440 ];
GMAT RAANview.CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT RAANview.ViewPointReference = Earth;
GMAT RAANview.ViewPointVector = [ 1800 0 15000 ];
GMAT RAANview.ViewDirection = Earth;
GMAT RAANview.ViewScaleFactor = 1;
GMAT RAANview.ViewUpCoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT RAANview.ViewUpAxis = X;
GMAT RAANview.CelestialPlane = Off;
GMAT RAANview.XYPlane = Off;

Creating and Configuring the Mission Sequence

Image of Mission Tree

The mission sequence presented here is relatively simple one. As said before, it is a good example of how to use loops, if statements, and targeting loops to achieve a goal. Again, this is not a perfect representation of how to efficiently implement low Earth orbit station keeping but it does work. How well it works and how 'tight' your orbit variation is will be up to you. Once you have implemented this version of the mission sequence, you may go back through and change the If statements so that they allow LEOsat to drift from its orbit more. This will increase the orbit's deviation but decrease the amount of fuel required.

  • Insert a While after Propagate1

    • Change the right hand side value to 10

  • After While1, insert another Propagate

    • Remove the propagate's stopping condition parameter and condition so that both fields are blank

  • Add the first of two If statements now

    • Change the left hand side to LEOsat.Earth.SMA

    • Change the right hand side to 6738.5

  • Insert a Target at this point

  • Append this with a Vary, a Maneuver, and an Achieve

    • Change the Goal to LEOsat.Earth.SMA

    • Set the Value as 6738.951134009997

    • Set the Tolerance as 0.05

  • Insert another If after EndIf1

    • Set the left hand side as LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.RAAN

    • Change the right hand side to 279.709

    • Add an '|' symbol under the 'If' to continue the statement

    • Set the left hand side of this second expression to the same LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.RAAN

    • Set the Condition as greater than, '>'

    • Add 279.949 as the right hand side value

  • Insert a final propagate after If2

    • Set the stopping condition parameter as LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.VZ

  • Insert the last target now

  • Append this target with another set of vary, maneuver, and achieve so as to match the previous sequence

    • Change the Variable of Vary2 to DefaultIB.N

    • Also set the lower of Vary 2 as -3.14159

    • LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.RAAN should be the Goal for Achieve2

    • 279.829547746 is Achieve2's Value

Script Syntax:

Propagate LEOprop(LEOsat) {LEOsat.ElapsedSecs = 8640.0};
While LEOsat.ElapsedDays < 10
   Propagate LEOprop(LEOsat);
   If LEOsat.Earth.SMA < 6738.5
      Target DC1;
         Vary DC1(DefaultIB.V = 0.5, {Perturbation = 0.0001, MaxStep = 0.2, Lower = 0, Upper = 3.14159});
         Maneuver DefaultIB(LEOsat);
         Achieve DC1(LEOsat.Earth.SMA = 6738.951134009997, {Tolerance = 0.05});
      EndTarget;  % For targeter DefaultDC
   EndIf;
   If LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.RAAN < 279.709 | LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.RAAN > 279.949
      Propagate LEOprop(LEOsat) {LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.VZ = 0.0};
      Target DC1;
         Vary DC1(DefaultIB.N = 0.5, {Perturbation = 0.0001, MaxStep = 0.2, Lower = -3.14159, Upper = 3.14159});
         Maneuver DefaultIB(LEOsat);
         Achieve DC1(LEOsat.EarthMJ2000Eq.RAAN = 279.829547746, {Tolerance = 0.1});
      EndTarget;  % For targeter DefaultDC
   EndIf;
EndWhile;

Figure: Propagate1 Propagate Command

Figure: While1 While Command

Figure: If1 If Command

Figure: Vary1 Vary Command

Figure: Achieve1 Achieve Command

Running the Mission

Image of Output Tree

The views that you created are good for seeing how well the mission sequence is keeping LEOsat in its orbit. The SMA view shows some thickness to it while the RAAN view shows barely any at all. You may now try and change the mission parameters as outlined in the mission tree section to see how the spacecraft's drift is affected.

Figure: Output

Spacecraft

Spacecraft Overview

This was created using the July 2, 2008 build of GMAT.

Overview

All of the tabs within the spacecraft object are listed below as links. To achieve a better overall understanding of the spacecraft's functions and properties, continue through the links to read through general definitions and explanations of the GUI dialog boxes, script syntax, and HTML quick reference tables.

Orbit Tab

Overview

The Spacecraft object's Orbit tab controls the state of the spacecraft at the given epoch. The state can be set in reference to any defined coordinate system and in several representations (Cartesian, Keplerian, etc.), with automatic conversions if either is changed.

Interfaces

Figure: Default name and settings for the Spacecraft Orbit panel

Create Spacecraft DefaultSC;
GMAT DefaultSC.DateFormat = UTCGregorian;
GMAT DefaultSC.Epoch = '01 Jan 2000 11:59:28.000';
GMAT DefaultSC.CoordinateSystem = EarthMJ2000Eq;
GMAT DefaultSC.DisplayStateType = Keplerian;
GMAT DefaultSC.SMA = 7191.938817629013;
GMAT DefaultSC.ECC = 0.02454974900598138;
GMAT DefaultSC.INC = 12.85008005658097;
GMAT DefaultSC.RAAN = 306.6148021947984;
GMAT DefaultSC.AOP = 314.190551535992;
GMAT DefaultSC.TA = 99.88774933204884;

Field Descriptions

State Type

Default: Cartesian.

Options: { Cartesian, Keplerian, ModifiedKeplerian, SphericalAZFPA, SphericalRADEC, Equinoctial }.

The State Type field allows the user to configure the type of state vector that they wish to use. The State Type field has a dependency upon the Coordinate System field. If the coordinate system chosen by the user does not have a gravitational body at the origin, then the state types Keplerian, ModifiedKeplerian, and Equinoctial are not permitted. This is because these state types require a µ value.

Units: N/A.

Coordinate System

Default: EarthMJ2000Eq.

Options: { EarthMJ2000Eq, EarthMJ2000Ec, EarthFixed, or any user defined system }

The Coordinate System field allows the user to choose which coordinate system with which to define the orbit state vector. The Coordinate System field has a dependency upon the State Type field. If the coordinate system chosen by the user does not have a gravitational body at the origin, then the state types Keplerian, ModifiedKeplerian, and Equinoctial are not permitted. This is because these state types require a µ value.

Units: N/A.

Epoch Format

Default: TAIModJulian.

Options: { A1ModJulian, TAIModJulian, UTCModJulian, TTModJulian, A1Gregorian, TAIGregorian, UTCGregorian, TTGregorian }

The Epoch Format field allows the user to specify the format for defining a spacecraft's initial epoch. Epoch Format determines both the time system (TAI, TT, etc) and the time format (Modified Julian or Gregorian).

Units: N/A.

Epoch

Default: 21545.000000000.

Options: { See Comments }

The Epoch field allows the user to specify the initial spacecraft epoch. The format of the epoch must be consistent with the Epoch Format field. If Epoch Format is of the "ModJulian" type, then the epoch is in Modified Julian format. If Epoch Format is a "Gregorian" type, the epoch is format like 01 Jan 2000 12:00:00.000. The epoch must be 04 Oct 1957 12:00:00.000 or later in all time systems (6116.0 ModJulian).

Units: Modified Julian - days, Gregorian - N/A.

The Modified Julian date offset is 2430000.0, which is different from the IAU's standard offset.

Cartesian State Type

X

Default: 7100.

Options: { Real Number }

X is the x-component of the Spacecraft state in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field.

Units: km.

Y

Default: 0.

Options: { Real Number }

Y is the y-component of the Spacecraft state in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field.

Units: km.

Z

Default: 1300.

Options: { Real Number }

Z is the z-component of the Spacecraft state in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field.

Units: km.

VX

Default: 0.

Options: { Real Number }

VX is the x-component of the Spacecraft velocity in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field.

Units: km/sec.

VY

Default: 7.35.

Options: { Real Number }

VY is the y-component of the Spacecraft velocity in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field.

Units: km/sec.

VZ

Default: 1.0.

Options: { Real Number }

VZ is the z-component of the Spacecraft velocity in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field.

Units: km/sec.

NOTE: Default values for the remaining state types are obtained through transformations of the default Cartesian spacecraft state values. The Keplerian, ModifiedKeplerian, and Equinoctial are dependant on the origin of the CoordinateSystem, because the state types require a µ value.

Keplerian State Type

SMA

Default: 7191.938817629013.

Options: { abs(SMA) > 1 meter }

The SMA field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating Keplerian semimajor axis in the coordinate system chosen in the Spacecraft Coordinate System field. SMA must be strictly greater than 1 m or less than -1 m to avoid numerical issues in the conversions to other state types. For circular and elliptical orbits ( 0 <= ECC < 0.9999999 ) SMA should only be greater than 1 m and for hyperbolic orbits (ECC > 1.0000001) SMA should be less than -1 m. GMAT does not support the creation of parabolic orbits.

Units: km.

ECC

Default: 0.02454974900598137.

Options: { 0.0 <= ECC <= 0.9999999, or ECC >= 1.0000001}

The ECC field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating eccentricity. For circular or elliptic orbits, ECC must be greater than or equal to 0.0, and less than or equal to 0.9999999 to avoid numerical issues in the conversion to other state types as the Keplerian elements are undefined for parabolic orbits. For hyperbolic orbits ECC must be greater than or equal to 1.0000001. See also the SMA description.

Units: Dimensionless.

INC

Default: 12.85008005658097.

Options: { Real Number }

The INC field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating inclination, in degrees, with respect to the selected coordinate system.

Units: degrees.

RAAN

Default: 306.6148021947984.

Options: { Real Number }

The RAAN field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating right ascension of the ascending node, in degrees, with respect to the selected coordinate system.

Units: degrees.

AOP

Default: 314.1905515359921.

Options: { Real Number }

The AOP field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating argument of periapsis, in degrees, with respect to the selected coordinate system.

Units: degrees.

TA

Default: 99.8877493320488.

Options: { Real Number }

The TA field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating true anomaly.

Units: degrees.

Modified Keplerian State Type

RadPer

Default: 7015.378524789846.

Options: { Real Number > 0 }

The RadPer field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating radius of periapsis. RadPer must be greater than zero.

Units: km.

RadApo

Default: 7368.49911046818.

Options: { Real Number ~= 0 }

The RadApo field is the spacecraft orbit's osculating radius of apoapsis. RadApo must be strictly greater than or less than zero. When RadApo is negative, the orbit is hyperbolic.

Units: km.

INC

See the Keplerian state section for a description on this field.

AOP

See the Keplerian state section for a description on this field.

RAAN

See the Keplerian state section for a description on this field.

TA

See the Keplerian state section for a description on this field.

Spherical AZFPA State Type

Default: 7218.032973047435.

Options: { Real Number > 0 }

The RMAG field allows the user to set the magnitude of the spacecraft's position vector.

Units: km.

RA

Default: 0.

Options: { Real Number }

The RA field allows the user to set the spacecraft's right ascension.

Units: degrees.

DEC

Default: 10.37584492005105.

Options: { Real Number }

The DEC field allows the user to set the spacecraft's declination.

Units: degrees.

VMAG

Default: 7.417715281675348.

Options: { Real Number >= 0 }

The VMAG field allows the user to set the magnitude of the spacecraft's velocity.

Units: km/sec.

AZI

Default: 82.37742168155043.

Options: { Real Number }

The AZI field allows the user to set the spacecraft's azimuth angle.

Units: degrees.

FPA

Default: 88.60870365370448.

Options: { Real Number }

The FPA allows the user to set a spacecraft's flight path angle.

Units: degrees.

See the SphericalAZFPA state section for a description on this field.
